<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_272d9ce9-c2bb-44f1-86f7-839b8d95db38'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16051708588381092740">في حضور الوجدان تتألق معاني أحلام مستغانمي، وفي ذاكرة الجسد تتوج حضورها، حروفاً كلمات عبارات تتقاطر في حفل الغناء الروحي. موسيقاه الوطن المنبعث برغم الجراحات... مليون شهيد وثورة ومجاهد، وجزائر الثكلى بأبنائها تنبعث زوابع وعواصف الشوق والحنين في قلب خالد الرسام الذي امتشق الريشة بعد أن هوت يده التي حملت السلاح يوماً، والريشة والسلاح سيّان، كلاهما ريشة تعزف على أوتار الوطن. </span>
  <span id="freeText16051708588381092740" style="display:none">في حضور الوجدان تتألق معاني أحلام مستغانمي، وفي ذاكرة الجسد تتوج حضورها، حروفاً كلمات عبارات تتقاطر في حفل الغناء الروحي. موسيقاه الوطن المنبعث برغم الجراحات... مليون شهيد وثورة ومجاهد، وجزائر الثكلى بأبنائها تنبعث زوابع وعواصف الشوق والحنين في قلب خالد الرسام الذي امتشق الريشة بعد أن هوت يده التي حملت السلاح يوماً، والريشة والسلاح سيّان، كلاهما ريشة تعزف على أوتار الوطن. ففي فرنسا وعندما كان يرسم ما تراه عيناه، جسر ميرابو ونهر السين، وجد أن ما يرسمه هو جسراً آخر ووادياً آخر لمدينة أخرى هي قسنطينة، فأدرك لحظتها أنه في كل حال لا يرسم ما نسكنه، وإنما ما يسكننا. <br />وهل كانت أحلام مستغانمي تكتب ذاكرة الجسد أم أنها تكتب ذاكرة الوطن؟!! الأمر سيّان فما الجسد إلا جزء من الوطن وما الوطن إلا هذا الجسد الساكن فيه إلى الأبد. تتقاطر الذكرى مفعمة بروح الماضي الذي يأبى إلا الحضور في كل شيء متجسداً السي طاهر التي كما عرفها خالد طفلة رجل قاد خطواته على درب الكفاح؛ عرفها أنثى... كانت من الممكن أن تكون حبيبته، زوجته، ولكنها باتت زوجة في زواج لم يحضره، تلف الذكرى الصفحات، وتتهادى العبارات ممسكة بتلابيب الذكريات دون أن توقظ النفس ملل الحضور. الوطن والحبيبة يجتمعان، والثورة والحب ينصهران في بوتقة واحدة، ومزيجهما عطاء فكري، بعيد عن الخيال، للواقع أقرب، وللإنسان في صدق مشاعره وأحاسيسه أقرب وأقرب.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16051708588381092740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

      $('edition_17343496').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_17343496').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_17343496').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_17343496').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);

        });
      });

  <span id="freeText4411092747352586391" style="display:none">Read this novel couple of years ago and it's one of the finest books I've ever read..<br /><br />I remember how I marked like hundreds of pages cause of the many quotes I just loved..<br /><br />Ahlam Mostaghanmi has her unique writing style,in her novels it feels like it's not about the story, it's about her way of telling the story, the language she uses, the way she describes it, magical!...<br /><br />I remember how she described Khaled's injury, how he felt abt his lost arm, so touching, and I remembered her description specifically after the Jan25 revolution, as many Egyptians have lost their eyes in the rev., they became marked w/ this war injury as Khaled in the novel... recalling this specific part of the book in these days made the effect of the revolution and the sacrifice made in it even deeper... <br /><br />A brilliant Novel, a must read :)</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1302627506" />
    <a title="Sunny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5870882-sunny"><img alt="Sunny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578175278p2/5870882.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1302627506?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sunny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sunny" href="/user/show/5870882-sunny">Sunny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789774247347" href="/book/show/426499.Memory_in_the_Flesh">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5870882-sunny?shelf=arabic-literature">arabic-literature</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1302627506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15475747049641420849">Wow. I have not read a book like this in a long time. It reminded me of the nostalgic elements of the kite runner which was a book that I loved. It’s about an old ex Algerian revolutionary fighter who moved to Paris and becomes an artist. There he by chance meets the daughter of one of the leaders of the revolution and falls madly in love with her but his twice her age so it’s pretty much doomed from the start. Very normal and not that original right? Well right. But what makes this novel unique</span>
  <span id="freeText15475747049641420849" style="display:none">Wow. I have not read a book like this in a long time. It reminded me of the nostalgic elements of the kite runner which was a book that I loved. It’s about an old ex Algerian revolutionary fighter who moved to Paris and becomes an artist. There he by chance meets the daughter of one of the leaders of the revolution and falls madly in love with her but his twice her age so it’s pretty much doomed from the start. Very normal and not that original right? Well right. But what makes this novel unique was the strings the writer pulls. Like all amazing (not great) books it’s hard to put down exactly what is so special about the book. There are lots of lines which I underlined – many of them about unrequited love. in a way it reminded me of Goethe’s Sufferings of young werther as the protagonist is suffering almost from the start to the finish of the book. if there is any negative which I can give is that after a certain point it becomes a bit too much and you just want to slap the dude and get him to stop acting like a muppet. but you don’t … and you keep on reading. The start is incredible and its very gripping. its tales off in the middle slightly but picks up again at the end. very worth reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15475747049641420849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16780343234827503642">The writing is very poetic and the reflections on Algeria and Constantine over a 50 year period is fascinating. His portrait of modern Algeria where daughters are given in arranged marriages to corrupt officials because there is no other choices is particularly sad. He lives in Paris where he has become a famous painter. He loves his m</span>
  <span id="freeText16780343234827503642" style="display:none">The writing is very poetic and the reflections on Algeria and Constantine over a 50 year period is fascinating. His portrait of modern Algeria where daughters are given in arranged marriages to corrupt officials because there is no other choices is particularly sad. Also sad is the general disillusionment of Arabs and what has happened after their so-called freedom.<br />Khaled is a former fighter in the Algerian war of liberation. He lives in Paris where he has become a famous painter. He loves his memories of his old country and when he meets the daughter of his old revolutionary commander he is consumed with passion for her. <br />This book then goes on and on about his feelings, his love and hope for a future with her. It just needed a bit more balance between the portrait of Algeria and the portrait of love lost.</span>

<div id="review_195566031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195566031" />
    <a title="Manar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5980260-manar"><img alt="Manar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470808722p2/5980260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195566031?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manar" href="/user/show/5980260-manar">Manar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5980260-manar?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195566031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4330783470300093506"> What I love most about her novels is the way she writes. Simply, captivating! But, the problem with Ahlam as an author is the repetitions! I've read two of her novels and It's always the same story, same characters, same ending! I was bored half way through! Hence, the rating of three stars.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2833495089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2833495089" />
    <a title="Mirnes Alispahić" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43368601-mirnes-alispahi"><img alt="Mirnes Alispahić" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500813640p2/43368601.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2833495089?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mirnes Alispahić" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mirnes Alispahić" href="/user/show/43368601-mirnes-alispahi">Mirnes Alispahić</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408846407" href="/book/show/18632934-the-bridges-of-constantine">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2833495089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7111234752637747781">There are bridges which we cannot burn down after crossing them, because they stay inside us, like a memory. There are countries which we live and countries which live in us, so says Khaled. The one he lives in is France, against whom he fought in order the break her chains from Algiers, which is the one living in him. His language is French, the manacle he cannot free himself after all those years while Arabic is almost forgotten. Even his mistress is French, but the France gave him everything </span>
  <span id="freeText7111234752637747781" style="display:none">There are bridges which we cannot burn down after crossing them, because they stay inside us, like a memory. There are countries which we live and countries which live in us, so says Khaled. The one he lives in is France, against whom he fought in order the break her chains from Algiers, which is the one living in him. His language is French, the manacle he cannot free himself after all those years while Arabic is almost forgotten. Even his mistress is French, but the France gave him everything that Algiers didn't.<br /><br />He left it more than two decades ago, disappointed in the corruption and what was left from the homeland for which he lost his hand in the revolution. Now, he's a renowned painter. An exile in a foreign land, whose canvases reflect the longing for the fatherland even though he doesn’t speak out loud about it, and then, one night on his exhibition, she appears. Last time he saw her, she was a baby on his lap, daughter of a friend and commander, now a sensual woman who stirred his passion.<br /><br />It's a stream of consciousness novel told completely in second person in which Khaled talks to her, after all it is because of her that he writes this novel, in order to kill her and be liberated from here as she once told him: „we write novels to kill those whose existence has become burden. Those who we love“. 'Bridges of Constantine' are much more than just a love story, it goes beyond that. That story about the unconsumed love, passion between the painter and writer, desire he feels for her, it's only a metaphor for yearning after homeland because Hayat is not only a young woman in his life. She's the Constantine, the city of his birth, Algiers, Arabian world, postwar generation. A mother. Bridges of Constantine which connects the cliffs and gorges on upon which the city was built. She's the sum of his longing, desires, disappointments, sorrows, lies and hatred.<br /><br />Just as Ahmed Nurudin thinks of his brother, and along the way tumbles through his mind certain questions and doubts, so is Khaled thinking about the homeland and all of that which is burden to him, and because of that, this novel evokes memories of 'Dervish and Death', a novel by Meša Selimović, mainly because of the Oriental approach to certain topics. Through Khaled's thinking’s, Ahlem discusses about women rights and politics, intertwined with subtle erotic in a way only a poet can do, but also talks about hypocrisy of a culture, paradox in which they live and double standards. That's clear from the chapter in which Khaled returns to Constantine for the first time in order to be on her wedding and he walks through the streets of his home town and stops in front of the brothel which was visited by all men, in which the women hid, and then he hears the call to prayer from a nearby mosque. As Khaled brings his story to the end, due to his brothers tragic death and the miserable life he led, he realizes that he must go back and that the bridges of Constantine, eternal motif of his painting, calling for him and they will continue to do that, as long as he lives in foreign land.<br /><br />It's been a while since I read a novel powerful as this, in which the man in his fifties has represented himself so convincingly but is written by woman, at that time, in her thirties. Maybe because there's a lot of Ahlem's father in the character of Khaled, but her also. He was the part of the that generation which fought for freedom only to get disappointment while she's the part of the postwar generation.<br /><br />At the time of publishing, Ahlem had difficulties to prove that it was, indeed, her novel due to how convincingly it was written. Because of her poems, published in the collections before 'Bridges of Constantine', and themes she dealt with, she lost the ability to continue her studies in Algiers so she went to Paris to graduate.<br /><br />With her poetic style, she wrote an elegy of a generation which fought for the ideal, vanished under corruption and hypocrisy. A novel that must be read. <br /><br />*****************************************************************************<br /><br />Postoje mostovi koje ne možemo spaliti kada pređemo na drugu stranu istih, već ostaju u nama, kao sjećanje. Postoje države u kojima živimo i postoje one koje žive u nama, kako kaže Khaled. Ona u kojoj živi on je Francuska, protiv koje se borio da bi skinuo njene lance s Alžira, države koja živi u njemu. Njegov jezik je francuski, okov koji ne može da zbaci i poslije toliko godina dok je arapski gotovo zaboravljen. Čak mu je i ljubavnica Francuskinja, ali Francuska mu je dala sve što Alžir nije. Iz njega je otišao prije više od dvije decenije, razočaran u korupciju i ono što je postalo od domovine za koju je dao ruku. Sada je priznat slikar. Stranac u tuđoj zemlji na čijim se platnima oslikava čežnja za otadžbinom iako ne progovara o tome glasno, a onda se jedne večeri na njegovoj izložbi pojavljuje ona. Kada ju je posljednji put vidio, bila je dijete u njegovom krilu, kćerka prijatelja i komandanta, sada je senzualna žena koja mu je uzburkala strasti.<br /><br />Roman toka misli, ispričan u cijelosti iz drugog lica u kojem se Khaled obraća njoj, jer zbog nje piše taj roman, kako bi je ubio i tako je se oslobodio jer, kako mu je ona rekla jednom prilikom, „roman pišemo kada se želimo osloboditi onih koje volimo“, „Mostovi Konstantina“ puno je više od ljubavnog romana. Zapravo, ta priča o nekonzumiranoj ljubavi, strasti između dvoje umjetnika, čežnji koju on osjeća za njom, samo je metafora za žudnjom ka domovini jer Hayat nije samo žena. Ona je Konstantin, grad njegovog rođenja, Alžir, arapski svijet, poslijeratna generacija. Majka. Mostovi Konstantina koji povezuju litice na kojima je izgrađen. Ona je zbir njegovih čežnji, želja, razočarenja, tuga i mržnji.<br /><br />Baš kao što Ahmed Nurudin razmišlja o svom bratu i usput se sukobljava s raznim pitanjima, tako i Khaled razmišlja o domovini i svemu onome što ga muči, te zbog toga budi uspomene na Selimovićev „Derviš i smrt“, prvenstveno zbog orijentalnog pristupa određenim temama. Kroz Khaledova razmišljanja Ahlem se dotiče prava žena, politike, suptilne erotike na način kako to samo jedan pjesnik, u ovom slučaju pjesnikinja, može uraditi, ali piše i o licemjerju jedne kulture, paradoksu u kojem žive i dvostrukim mjerilima. To je najjasnije u poglavlju kada se Khaled vrati u Konstantin prvi put, kako bi prisustvovao njenom vjenčanju pa šeta ulicama rodnog grada da bi se zaustavio ispred vrata bordela koji su posjećivali svi muškarci, u koji su dolazile sve žene, a onda začuje ezan s obližnje džamije. Kako Khaled privodi kraju svoju priču, zbog bratove tragične smrti i žalosnog života, shvaća da se mora vratiti i da ga mostovi Konstantina, vječiti motiv njegovih slika, dozivaju sebi i nastavit će, dokle god živi na tuđoj zemlji.<br /><br />Odavno nisam pročitao tako moćan roman, u kojem se tako uvjerljivo predstavlja muškarac u pedesetim godinama kojeg je zapravo napisala žena, u to vrijeme, tridesetogodišnjakinja. Možda zbog toga što ovdje ima dosta njenog oca, u liku Khaleda, ali i nje. On je pripadao toj generaciji koja se borila za slobodu, samo da bi dobili razočarenje dok je ona dio te postratne generacije. Svojevremeno, Ahlem je zbog te uvjerljivosti jedva dokazala da je to doista njen roman. Ona je zbog pjesama, koje je izdala u zbirkama prije ovog romana, tematike kojom se bavila, ostala bez školovanja u Alžiru pa je isto nastavila u Parizu.<br /><br />Svojim poetičnim stilom, napisala je elegiju generacije koja se borila za ideale koji su nestali pod korupcijom i licemjerjem. Nešto što se mora pročitati.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7111234752637747781" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1089347260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089347260" />
    <a title="Molly Ison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15875470-molly-ison"><img alt="Molly Ison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470256666p2/15875470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089347260?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly Ison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly Ison" href="/user/show/15875470-molly-ison">Molly Ison</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408846407" href="/book/show/18632934-the-bridges-of-constantine">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15875470-molly-ison?shelf=one-country-one-book">one-country-one-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089347260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8311633370778293841">Once the protagonist was a fighter in the Algerian war for independence, but now he's an ex-pat and an artist, disgusted by the corruption in the country he left behind, obsessed with the daughter of his old commander whom he once loved as a daughter... Historical romance is a genre new to me and Algeria was a country new to me. It's hard to rate this as a book. It was hard for me to get really engrossed in the story and the prose didn't flow easily, but I'm not a big fan of romance and there mi</span>
  <span id="freeText8311633370778293841" style="display:none">Once the protagonist was a fighter in the Algerian war for independence, but now he's an ex-pat and an artist, disgusted by the corruption in the country he left behind, obsessed with the daughter of his old commander whom he once loved as a daughter... Historical romance is a genre new to me and Algeria was a country new to me. It's hard to rate this as a book. It was hard for me to get really engrossed in the story and the prose didn't flow easily, but I'm not a big fan of romance and there might have been translation issues. The writing felt very modern in sensibility and rather purple. It's hard to parse what if any of that was a uniquely Algerian attitude - fatalistic, dramatic, obsessive. I'm reading a book from every country and it's been a challenge to separate the universal from the specific. Despite not having an affinity for the genre, it was well worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8311633370778293841" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5091739135042658967" style="display:none">Poetic and very much the Arabic style of writing ( it is after all a translation of an original Algerian novel). <br /><br /><br />I think reading the book as an English reader it does come off long winded, full of cheese and ‘omg Khaled can we see some action and get to the point now my friend’ 😂 .<br /><br />Knowing some of how the Arabic language works and reading it from that point of view I thought this was really a sweet book. <br /><br />I think love in the Arab culture takes time to grow and nurture. <span id="freeTextContainer13251916480201890624">What a masterpiece of literature!<br/><br/>Although i love arabic language and find it unique, i rarely read arabic novels due to bad experience. this book ignited this love again with the author's great use of language better than anything i have ever read of contemporary literature; 400 pages were music to my ears regardless of the plot/ events.<br/><br/>If arabic language was a wild horse, Ahlam M is the tamer, if it was a song, she is the um kulthoum.<br/><br/>Style:<br/><br/>Captivating angry, passionate, disappointed and pessimi</span>
  <span id="freeText13251916480201890624" style="display:none">What a masterpiece of literature!<br /><br />Although i love arabic language and find it unique, i rarely read arabic novels due to bad experience. this book ignited this love again with the author's great use of language better than anything i have ever read of contemporary literature; 400 pages were music to my ears regardless of the plot/ events.<br /><br />If arabic language was a wild horse, Ahlam M is the tamer, if it was a song, she is the um kulthoum.<br /><br />Style:<br /><br />Captivating angry, passionate, disappointed and pessimistic voice through out the pages.<br /><br />Unconventional love story on the surface, paralleled with profound love and nostalgia for home town touching on politics, humanity and existentialism among other themes. The narrators lover and home town became one: his source of love, inspiration, and pain at the same time<br /><br />Made me want to write in arabic, at the same time it put my dream to write to shame by raising the bar too high.</span>

<div id="review_2871881941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2871881941" />
    <a title="Asaria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44427430-asaria"><img alt="Asaria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603708085p2/44427430.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2871881941?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asaria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asaria" href="/user/show/44427430-asaria">Asaria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9789992195444" href="/book/show/19397772-the-bridges-of-constantine">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44427430-asaria?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44427430-asaria?shelf=literature-arabic">literature-arabic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44427430-asaria?shelf=stars-5">stars-5</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2871881941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10015303748553744224">The Bridges of Constantine... Difficult love, it is, isn't it? It has been on my radar for at least year with one unsuccessful attempt in January. As usual, wrong book, wrong mood, wrong time. Possibly if I pushed myself to get through, I would have disliked it for the same reason I give it a high rating.<br/><br/>It is slow, reflective book, which takes time to immerse the reader in the content. Multilayered for sure, written in the first person too. However <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[there are hints that suggest th</span></span>
  <span id="freeText10015303748553744224" style="display:none">The Bridges of Constantine... Difficult love, it is, isn't it? It has been on my radar for at least year with one unsuccessful attempt in January. As usual, wrong book, wrong mood, wrong time. Possibly if I pushed myself to get through, I would have disliked it for the same reason I give it a high rating.<br /><br />It is slow, reflective book, which takes time to immerse the reader in the content. Multilayered for sure, written in the first person too. However <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[there are hints that suggest that the narrator might be unreliable  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Smart move from the author, because while she gives answers to some questions that might arise, this device also can explain any contradictions that would appear in the narrative.<br /><br />The narrative itself is centered around the complicated relationship of the narrator and Hayat. Somewhere around 20%, I realized that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ in his mind she, motherland and his home city became one  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. In an almost Mickiewicz' way: <br />"I and fatherland are one. My name is million, cause for million I love and suffer agonies" -"Our forefathers' Eve', Adam Mickiewicz<br />Of course, Mosteghanemi doesn't go so far, but not too far.<br /><br />The book is also exploring the role of artist and literature. The concept of author-prophet isn't foreign to me. That's something Polish writers were struggling in the past. In the early XIX century, prophet-writer was someone who leads the nation forward toward the future, a spiritual leader. In positivism era, he is an educator. Therefore, in this context author should be someone, who shows what others would like to remain hidden, breaks taboos, is a moral authority, full of dignity, questioner of the established order. That's a great burden on any shoulder, too great in my opinion. This perspective curiously intertwines with Mosteghanemi's novel.<br /><br />Overall, well translated, lyrical work. 4* upped to 5*, for causing emotional response in me.<br /><br />Onwards to the second book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10015303748553744224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6925828531409605187" style="display:none">Just finished reading "Memory In the Flesh" by Ahlam Mosteghanemi. <br /><br />As Algeria's most important female writer, she offers an insight into this former French colony from a unique perspective as the daughter of one of the heroes of the Algerian Revolution. <br /><br />As well as a different take than we would be offered by combatants on either side, her writings are a milestone as she is the first successful female novelist to write in Arabic (as my mastery of the language is virtually non-existent, I have had to settle for an English translation.) <br /><br />I appreciate having had the opportunity to gain a bit more understanding of this complex relationship between France and Algeria. Now, back to Steinbeck with "The Wayward Bus' from 1947.</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zCZv5P4BeEM2p5KCg6fY+5YzmV48Hmuloxt8luwLb8CA8xFNFtAiAFCp/ZRfScJVXDFl43OaRJMtAOrUXMlWsA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rGoSp3qRELCoVXnrtjygyR9LUPtGr8vjRUuZSVwbJ0jgv2wOkkBK885bFv1q0rpn1UmsRgkr5NXLUA8L7NkeOA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

وعطائها الذي لا حدود له للمحبوب: &quot;كنت على استعداد لأن أصغر فتكبر..لأن أفشل لتنجح، لأن أخبو لتلمع..&quot;، ونوعية حبها الذي لا يقدره بل يتجاهله أو يقوم باستغلاله لصالح أهداف أقل أهمية منه بكثير، وأقل قيمة. &quot;ما زلت لا أدرك، لا أدرك كيف يتلاعب رجل بامرأة تحبه من دون أن يخاف للحظة مما يفعله نحوها!&quot;\n\nفي كل مرة و&quot;بعد كل خيبة أمل.. بعد كل محنة وكل نزوة.. كنت أحاول لملمة أجزائي لما حدث كل هذا.. أتكون أنت عقابي على مغادرة وطن أحبني!..&quot;، وفكرة العقاب والثواب التي يسخر منها عزيز، تؤمن هي بها: &quot;مؤمنة أنا بيوم الحساب أكثر من أي شيء،&quot; لأنها تأمل عبرها أن ينال عزيز عقابه على ما اقترفه بحقها.\n\nقالت لهما العجوز الهندية غريبة الأطوار، دون سابق معرفة: &quot;هي متعبة منك..منك فقط..وأنت متعب من كل شيء..&quot;، وقالت لها &quot;هيفاء&quot; صديقتها الكويتية التي تتخاصم دائما وعزيز، بأنه لا يستحقها، وتقول جمانة له اليوم &quot;حبي لك كان أعمى يا عزيز..وأن هيفاء رأت فيك ما لم أره..&quot;، رأت الكذب المتسلسل والخيانة والإنكار الذي يشكك الآخر بنفسه وبعقله وإحساسه، وهي صفات تتجاهلها المرأة التي تحب رجلاً يحبها لكنه غير قادر على الالتزام بها. قال لها بصراحة: &quot;اسمعي.. أنا رجل لعوب.. أشرب وأعربد وأعاشر النساء.. لكنني أعود إليك في كل مرة..&quot;، وكانت تتحمل الأذى: &quot;تؤذينني عمداً وكأنك تفرغ في نفسي أحقادك وأوجاعك وأمراضك، تؤذيني عمداً باسم الحبّ..&quot;. وهي بالرغم من كل الحقائق والوقائع تعترف: &quot;لم أبكِ بحرقة إلا بسببك ولم أضحك من أعماقي إلا معك.. يخشى منك في الوقت ذاته..&quot;\n\nكيف يلتقيان، وهو يؤمن بأن الغاية تبرر الوسيلة، وهي تؤمن &quot;بأن الوسيلة أحياناً أهم من الغاية!&quot;؟\n\n&quot;قلت لي يوماً بأن حكايات الحبّ الشرقية غالباً ما تنتهي <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4653511"><img alt="رجال في الشمس" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1321707850l/4653511._SX98_.jpg" />

<script>

p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.17 avg rating &mdash; 17,015 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1963\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer9624388514243288907\">يمثل غسان كنفاني مؤلف هذه الرواية نموذجاً خاصاً للكاتب السياسي \nوالروائي والقاص والناقد، فكان مبدعاً في كتاباته كما كان مبدعاً في حياته ونضاله واستشهاده. وقد نال عام 1966 جائزة أصدقاء الكتاب في لبنان \"لأفضل رواية عن روايته\" ما تبقى لكم كما نال جائزة <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText9624388514243288907\" style=\"display:none\">يمثل غسان كنفاني مؤلف هذه الرواية نموذجاً خاصاً للكاتب السياسي \nوالروائي والقاص والناقد، فكان مبدعاً في كتاباته كما كان مبدعاً في حياته ونضاله واستشهاده. وقد نال عام 1966 جائزة أصدقاء الكتاب في لبنان &quot;لأفضل رواية عن روايته&quot; ما تبقى لكم كما نال جائزة منظمة الصحافيين العالمية (I.O.J) عام 1974، ونال جائزة &quot;اللوتس&quot; التي يمنحها اتحاد كتاب آسيا وأفريقيا عام 1975. وتعد روايته رجال في الشمس التي صدرت في بيروت عام 1963 من أوائل الأعمال الروائية الفلسطينية التي تكتب عن التشرد والموت والحيرة. وفيها يروي حكاية ثلاثة فلسطينيين من أجيال مختلفة، يلتقون حول ضرورة إيجاد حل فردي لمشكلة الإنسان الفلسطيني <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9520426943874965005">Ahlam Mosteghanemi (Arabic: <a> أحلام مستغانمي </a>) is an Algerian author and the first female Algerian author of Arabic-language works to be translated into English. <br/>By the time she was born, Mosteghanemi's father had already been imprisoned after the 1945 riots. When the Algerian war broke out in 1954, her family home in Tunisia became a central meeting point for resistance fighters allied to the Alge</span>
  <span id="freeText9520426943874965005" style="display:none">Ahlam Mosteghanemi (Arabic: <a> أحلام مستغانمي </a>) is an Algerian author and the first female Algerian author of Arabic-language works to be translated into English. <br />By the time she was born, Mosteghanemi's father had already been imprisoned after the 1945 riots. When the Algerian war broke out in 1954, her family home in Tunisia became a central meeting point for resistance fighters allied to the Algerian People’s Party including her father and cousins. After independence, in 1962, the family returned to Algeria, where Mosteghanemi was sent to the country’s first Arabic-language school.<br />In the late 1960s and early 1970s, she became one of the first Algerian Arabic writers, broadcasting her poetry on national radio to support her family due to her father’s ill-health. She earned a B.A. in Arabic Literature from the University of Algiers in 1973, and also published her first poetry collection, Ala’ Marfa Al Ayam (the harbour of days).<br />In 1982, she received her Ph.D. in Sociology from the Sorbonne in Paris (her thesis was published by L’Harmattan as Algerie, Femmes et l’Ecriture), where she had moved in the late 1970s. <br />She married a Lebanese journalist and moved to Beirut, where she published her first novel, Memory in the Flesh (Zakirat al Jassad) in 1993. To date, it has sold over a million copies across the Arabic-speaking world. It was translated into English by the American University in Cairo Press in 2000, after winning the 1998 Naguib Mahfouz Medal for Literature.<br />Ahlem Mosteghanemi currently lives in Beirut, Lebanon with her husband and has 3 children.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9520426943874965005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

لقائي به، وضمة منه احتضنت فيها التاريخ والحبّ معاً، فقد كان نصفه سي الطاهر ونصفه حياة. كانت شقته على بساطتها مؤثثة بدفء عن استعاض بالأثاث الجميل عن خسارة ما، ومن استعان بالموسيقى القسنطينية ليغطي على نواح داخلي لا يتوقف... رحت أسأل ناصر عن أخباره وعن سفره من ألمانيا إلى باريس إن كان وجد فيه مشقة. ردّ مازحاً: كانت الأسئلة أطول من المسافة! ثم أضاف أقصد الإهانات المهذبة التي تقدم إليك من المطارات على شكل أسئلة قال مراد مازحاً: واش تريد يا خويا..&quot; وجه الخروف معروف&quot;! ردّ ناص: معروف بماذا؟ بأنه الذئب؟ أجاب مراد: إن لم تكن الذئب، فالذئاب كثيرة هذه الأيام. ولا أرى سبباً لغضبك. هنا على الأقل لا خوف عليك ما دمت بريئاً. ولا تشكل خطراً على الآخرين. أما عندنا فحتى البريء لا يضمن سلامته! ردّ ناصر متذمراً: نحن نفاصل بين موت وآخر، وذلّ وآخر، لا غير. في الجزائر يبحثون عنك لتصفيتك جسدياً. عذابك يدوم زمن اختراق رصاصة. في أوروبا بذريعة إنقاذك من القتلة يقتلونك عرياً كل لحظة، ويطيل من عذابك أن العري لا يقتل بل يجردك من حميميتك ويغتالك مهانة. تشعر أنك تمشي بين الناس وتقيم بينهم لكنك لن تكون منهم، أنت عارٍ ومكشوف ومشبوه بسبب اسمك، وسحنتك ودينك. لا خصوصية لك برغم أنك في بلد حر. أنت تحب وتعمل وتسافر وتنفق بشهادة الكاميرات وأجهزة التنصت وملفات الاستخبارات&quot;. \nفي زمن موت كرامة العربي، في زمن تهميشه في زمن احتقاره وامتهانه تضحي مساحة سرديات أحلام مستغانمي أوسع وأعمق، وبعيدة كل البعد عن روتينية الصنعة الروائية في استرسالاتها في انبعاثات أحداثها. فهي تؤدي مهمة تتجاوز الحدث، مخنوقة النفس العربية عموماً، الجزائرية على وجه الخصوص، مستلهمة من الواقع منولوجاتها الداخلية وحتى الخارجية، ممتزجة باليأس، وغارقة في لجج من الإحباطات. تسترسل أحلام مستغانمي في انسياحاتها السردية متماهية مع الجزائري مع العربي في آلامه وأوجاعه. في محاولة لتشخيص مرض وإيجاد علاج. من خلال أسلوب أدبي رائع، وعبارات ومعانٍ تميل إلى الرمز حيناً، إلى الواقعية أحاييناً مستدرجة مشاعر القارئ وفكره للتماهي في رحلتها
